Quan endeve ad alcu tremor per freg en le nervi o per febre de causa frega, o per autra causa semblant, lahoras cove que tu cauterises aquel am quatre cauteris o am v sobre les spondils del dos, entre quascun spondilh am un cauteri; e am cauteri en le pietz de lu, e sobre l‘estomac de lu, am cauteri olivar.	When there is a trembling in some part due to irritation of the nerves or due to fever caused by irritability, or for other similar cause, then it is good that you cauterize that with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra an individual cautery; and also on the feet of it, and on the stomach of it, with olive cautery.
E la tremor de lu se repausa e festina la sanetat de la malautia frega.	And then the trembling subsides and hastens the healthiness of the irritated disease.
Capitol .lv.	Chapter 55.
De cauterizacio de albati accidentz al cors.	On the Cauterization of Accidental Bleedings in the Body.
Quan en le cors so espellitz albati, e so pustulas fendas las quals so feytas de materias grossas corruptas; donc cove al comensament cum apareyso, que sia cauterizat sobre tot cap de la fistola am cauteri subtil am fustz de mirt, la extremitat del qual es estenduda am foc; o am razitz de erestologia longua; o am cauteri lentecular.	When in the body there are accidental bleedings and pustules that open up into wounds which are made of gross, corrupted matters; then it is good at first sight as appears, to be cauterized all over the head of the fistula with a subtle cautery made from myrtle wood, the extremity of which is extended by fire; or with the roots of long-lived estrogia; or with lentecular cautery.
E alscunas veguadas es cauteri ademamil al comensament de la sua expulcio segon aquesta manieyra; e no so cregudas, e es disrumpuda la superfluitat fazens aquels, et sana de aquels.	And sometimes it is good to cauterize at the beginning of its expulsion according to this manner; and not to be believed, and thus the superfluity is dispelled from those things, and they are healed.
Mays empero cove que aquo sia fayt aprop evacuacio am fleubotomia.	But nonetheless it is good that this should be done with proper evacuation by phlebotomy.
Capitol lvi.	Chapter 56.
De cauterizacio de fluex de sanc accident per incisio de arceria.	On the Cauterization of Accidental Bleeding from Incision of Archeria.
Tropas veguadas endeve fluex de arceria que es inciza deves la plagua la qual endeve deforo, o deves la incizio de apostemas o cauteri del membre, e alor semblantz, e es dificil remaura aquel.	Many times there occurs bleeding from archeria which is caused by the wound that needs to be cut away, or by the incision of apostemes or cauteries of the member, and thus it resembles, and it is difficult to cure that.
Donc cum accideys ad alcu aquo, lahoras tu·t coyta am la tua ma a l’orrifici de la arceria, e pausa sobre aquel le tieu dit endic estrenh aquel motas veguadas entro que sia ostat le fluex del sanc dejos le tieu dit, e que non yesqua.	Therefore, as it happens to some of these things, then you should take a piece of cloth with your hand and place it on the orifice of the archeria, and pause above that which I have said to strengthen that many times until the flow of blood is stopped by what I have said, and there be no more.
E aprop pausa en le foc les cauteris olivars paucs e grantz, per nombre motz, e exsuffla sobre aquels entro que sian mot ignitz.	And then pause in the fire with olive cauteries, small and great, by number of moles, and blow upon them until they are quite ignited.
E aprop pren de aquels un petit o un gran segon le loc e la plagua en la qual es rompuda la arteria, sobre aquela vena festinantment pus que auras remaugut le tieu dit, e te le cauteri entro que sia abcindit e restreyt aquel sanc.	And then take from those one small or one great according to the location and wound in which the artery is broken, on that vein which hastens more than you will have restored what I have said, and place the cautery until it is abscinded and restrained that blood.
E si le sanc es expellit de l’orrifici de la arteria quan tu remaues le tieu dit e extringeys le cauteri, lahoras pren la un autre cauteri coytadament dels cauteris les quals en le foc son preparatz, e donc no cesses fer aquo un aprop autre entro que le sanc sia restrengit.	And if the blood is expelled from the orifice of the artery when you remove what I have said and extinguish the cautery, then take another cautery carefully from the cauteries which are prepared in the fire, and thus do not cease to do this again until the blood is restrained.
E guarda te que no comburas le nervi que aqui es, e que vengua sobre le malaute autra malicia.	And beware that you do not burn the nerves which are here, and that another evil comes upon the patient.
E sapias que quan de l’arteria flueys sanc, lahoras no es possible en aquels restrenge la sanc, e majorment quan l’arteria es gran, si no am una de quatre manieyras: o am cauteri ayssi quo dit havem, o am extraccio quan no es extrayta, quar quan es extrayta las extremitatz de lu miels son comburidas e es restreyt le sanc, o que sia liat am fiel o am liament per fort strectura, o que sian pausadas sobre lu medicinas de las quals la vertut es restringir la sanc; e sian strengudas am pulvinar am costriccio decent.	And know that when blood flows from the artery, it is not possible to restrain the blood in those places, and especially when the artery is large, unless by one of four methods: or with a cautery as we have said, or with extraction when it is not extracted, because when it is extracted the extremities are burnt off and the blood is restrained, or that it be tied with a thread or with a ligament by strong constriction, or that certain medicines be applied to it which have the virtue of restraining the blood; and they should be strengthened with poultice and decent compression.
Mays aquel que aministra restriccio decent de lu am liament e am strictura am draps o per posicio de causas comburentz e de semblantz, no comfereys sino tart.	But he who administers decent restraint of it with ligature and constriction by means of cloths or through the position of causes that burn and resemble, does not conform except later.
Mays si aquo endeve ad alcu e no sia le metge present ni medicina, lahoras obre am pausament del dit indic sobre le orrifici de aquela vena ayssi cum havem dit, e entenda a la gran costreccio de lu entro que le sanc sia ostat de la sobirana partida de la plagua, e sobre la arceria le dit no sia remaugut; e de sobre la arceria sia aspergit am aygua frega de mot gran fregiditat entro que·l sanc sia congilat e engrossat; e mays cossire en que ha de cauteri o de medicina necessitat.	But if this happens to someone and there is no doctor present or medicine, then take a pause from the indicated digit on the orifice of that vein as we have said, and understand by great constriction of it until the blood is stopped from the supreme part of the wound, and above the archery the same thing is not restored; and above the archery be sprinkled with cold water of very great coolness until the blood is congealed and thickened; and also consider in what there is need for a cautery or medicine.
Comensa la segonda partida.	The second part begins.
De incisio e perforacio e ventozas e de fleubotomia e de plaguas e de lor semblants.	On the Cutting and Piercing and Vents and Bloodletting and Wounds and their Likenesses.
Aquestas son paraulas de Albucazis.	These are the words of Albucasis.
Ja havem dit en le primier capitol tota malautia en la qual cauteri am foc es convenient e am medicina comburent, e las occasios e las causas de lu, e les instrumentz en aquels necessaris am las formas dels cauteris; e he ordenatz les capitols de la subiranetat del cap entro als pes.	We have already said in the first chapter about every disease in which cautery with fire is convenient and with medicine that burns, and the occasions and causes of it, and the instruments necessary in those places with the forms of the cauteries; and we have arranged the chapters of the subordination of the head down to the feet.
E yeu procesire en aquest capitol per aquela meteysa guisa, per que sia alliujat lo querent aquo, lahoras sobre aquo que aura demandat.	And you will proceed in this chapter by that same manner, so that it may be clarified for whoever desires this, as you have requested.
E denant que yeu comense aquo, cove, fils, que aprenguatz que en aquest capitol es per terror aquo que es en le capitol primier de cauterizacio.	And before you begin this, it is good, son, that you learn that in this chapter, it is about the same thing as is in the first chapter of cautery.
E per aquo que cove que sia en lu gran cautela, quar en la operacio la qual es en aquest capitol motas veguadas catz evacuacio la qual es am sanc am le qual esta la vida deves la aspersio de la vena o incisio sobre l’apostema o apercio de exsitura o puracio de la plagua o extraccio de sageta o incizio de peyra e a lor semblantz.	And therefore it is necessary to be in great caution, for in the operation which is in this chapter many times blood evacuation occurs, which is with blood that contains life; and thus one must be cautious about the sprinkling of the vein or incision on the apostema or appearance of exiture or purgation of the wound or extraction of sagette or incision of peyra and their likenesses.
E de totz aquels so acompanhatz temor e tremor e en le mas de lor catz la mort.	And all those things are accompanied by fear and trembling, and in the most of them death.
E yeu amonesti vos que sobre vos no caia aquo en le qual es esitacio, quar alcunas veguadas cazo deves vos manieyras de homes am manieyras motas de malautias.	And I warn you that over yourselves this should not fall, for sometimes the case requires methods of men with many methods of diseases.
E de lor es alcu que s’irays am la sua malautia e es leugiera deves lu la mort, e aysso per la vehemensia de aquo que troba de sa malautia, e per longuesa de la malautia de lu, e am la malautia es paor la qual significa mort.	And among them are those who rush with their own disease and it is light for them to die, and thus because of the vehemence of what they find in their disease, and because of the length of their disease, and with their disease there is fear which means death.
E de aquels es le qual dona a tu son aver e ditta, tu esperant am aquel sanetat, e la sieua malautia es perniciosa.	And among them is one who gives to you his own breath and takes away from you, you hoping for health with him, and his disease is mortal.
E donc no cove que tu consentas en aquel que ve a vos del qual es aquesta manieyra; e la vostra cautela sia major que covesitat e la vostra rapacitat; e no presumatz alcuna causa sobre aquo sino aprop sciencia certa la qual virifica aquo deves vos, e al qual perve successio lausabla.	And therefore it is not good that you consent to that which comes to you from whom this manner is; and your caution should be greater than covetousness and rapacity; and do not presume any cause about this except proper certain science which verifies what you know, and through which succession praiseable.
E usatz en la curacio de totz vostres malautes de pronosticacio e indicacio de lu al qual es salut convertida, quar en aquel es a vos ajutori sobre adquisicio de fama e de memoria, de lausor e de gloria.	And use in the cure of all your diseases prophetic and indicative science, which is converted to health, for in that is help to you over the acquisition of fame and memory, praise and glory.
O, filhs, Dieus en vos spire le sieu entendement e no oste a vos direccio e proteccio, quar aquo es en la sua ma.	Oh, sons, God inspires in you His own understanding and does not withhold from you direction and protection, for this is in His hand.
E yeu e ordenat aquest capitol distingent per capitols segon que precedit en le capitol de cauteris, de la cura del cap entro als pes, per que sia a vos alleujat aquo que demandatz de aquo e del qual havetz necessitat.	And I have ordered this chapter distinct by chapters according to what preceded in the chapter of cauteries, from the cure of the head down to the feet, so that it may be alleviated for you that which you ask about and of which you have need.
Capitol primier.	Chapter One.
De la curacio de aygua la qual es contenguda en le cap dels enfantz.	On the Cure of Water Contained in the Head of Children.
Sapias que aquesta malautia motas veguadas endeve als enfantz deves le enfantament e quan la noyrissa estrenh le cap del enfant ses livitat.	Know that this disease often occurs in children during the time of birth, and when the umbilical cord is tightly tied around the child's head.
E alcunas veguadas endeve per causa amaguada la qual no es saubuda.	And sometimes it occurs due to a hidden cause that is not known.
Mays yeu no vi aquesta malautia sino en les enfantz; e a totz aquels les quals yeu vi se coytec la mort, e per ayssi es a mi vist layssada obra en aquels.	But I have never seen this disease except in children; and all those whom I have seen are on the verge of death, and therefore it is to me a pitiful sight.
E yeu e vist que un enfant le cap del qual era d’aygua omplit, e·l cap de lu era totjorn ayssi magnificat entro que ceser no podia sobre si meteys per la grandesa del sieu cap, e mays que la humiditat fe aucmentada entro que foc mort.	And I have seen that a child whose head was filled with water, and his head was always magnificently expanded to the point where he could not even move on his own due to the greatness of his head, and more so that the humidity increased until it became mortal.
E aquesta humiditat o es agreguada entre la codena e l’os, o es agreguada dejos le os sobre le ciphac.	And this humidity either accumulates between the vertebrae and the bone, or accumulates behind the bone above the skull.
Quar la operacio en aquel si la humiditat es entre la codena e l’os e le apostema es pauc, lahoras cove que tu fendas en le mieg loc del cap am una fissura en la latitut, e sia la longitut de la fissura cays dos notz entro que corra la humiditat, e aquesta es la forma del spatum:	Therefore the operation in that case is to make an incision in the middle of the head with a fissure in the latitude, and the length of the fissure should be about two inches until the humidity flows, and this is the form of the spatula.
E donc si la humiditat es mays augmentada e l’apostema es major, lahoras son aqui dos fissuras segon aquesta manieyra:	And therefore if the humidity is further increased and the apostema is greater, then there are two incisions according to this manner:
E si la humiditat es dejos le os, senhal de lu es que tu vezes la comissuras del cap ubertas de tota partida e l’aygua es spremuda quan tu compremes aquela am la tieua ma a las partidas dedintz e no es aquo a tu amaguat.	And if the humidity is behind the bone, then the sign of it is that you should press the commissures of the head on all sides and the water will be squeezed out when you compress that with your hand inwards and not to your surprise.
Cove que tu fendas en le mieg loc del cap am tres fissuras segon aquesta manieyra:	It is good for you to make an incision in the middle of the head with three incisions according to this manner:
e aprop la inscizio extratz ne tota la humiditat; e aprop strenh las fissuras am draps e plumassols; e aprop enbroca aquo de sobre am vi e oli entro al quint dia, e aprop deslia le liament e cura la plagua am tentas e enguentz, e strenh le cap am equalitat; e mange le malaute am vianda secca de pauca humiditat entro que·l membre sia confortat e sanat.	And then make an incision in the middle of the head with three incisions according to this manner: and appropriate extract all the humidity from the wound; and then strengthen the incisions with cloths and poultices; and then envelop it with a covering made of vinegar and oil within five days, and then untie the ligature and cure the wound with tentes and unguents, and strengthen the head with equality; and feed the patient with dry food of little humidity until the member is comforted and healed.
E es autra manieyra de incisio, que consideras hon apar la magnitut del apostema e la colleccio de l’aygua, quar alcunas veguadas es mays en le occipicii, o en la partida denant, o en la destra, o en la sinistra; e donc aten am la incizio on appar le apostema e la replecio de l’aygua, e fen aquo segon que a tu es miels possible.	And there is another manner of incision, which considers how the magnitude of the apostema and the collection of water appear, for sometimes it appears more in the occiput, or in the front part, or on the right side, or on the left side; and therefore attend to the incision where the apostema appears and the accumulation of water is seen, and make it according to what seems best to you.
Et observa que no inscindas la arteria e endevengua flueys de sanc e mora le malaute per aquel flux de sanc am evacuacio de humiditat.	And observe that you do not cut the artery and thus blood flows and the patient dies from that flow of blood with evacuation of humidity.
Capitol .ii.	Chapter II.
De inscisio de las arterias las quals so aprop las aurelhas, apeladas hilasseysse.	On the Incision of the Arteries which are near the Ears, called Hilarseysse.
Capitol segon.	Chapter Three.
Quan endeveno ad alcu catars o raumas als huelhs o al pietz, e es antiquat aquo, e no confereys en aquo la curacio de las medicinas, lahoras la deriera curacio en aquest es incizio de aquelas dos arterias.	When you find some catarrh or rash on the eyes or feet, and it is old, and there is no conformity in that with the cure of medicines, then the last resort in this case is to cut those two arteries.
E donc cove quan tu vols inscidir aquelas que le malaute raza lo sieu cap, e aprop fregua le loc am drap aspre per so que aparan las arcerias, e aprop sia strengut le col del malaute am alcu drap; e aprop considera on polsa la vena; e les locs de quascuna sobre les locs les quals so aprop las aurelhas depremutz, e tant se occultan sino en alcus homes.	And therefore when you want to cut those that the patient's head is filled with water, and then apply a rough cloth to the location where the arteries appear, and then strengthen the patient's neck with some cloth; and then consider which vein pulsates; and the locations of each one are on the locations which are near the ears, repressed, and only in some men.
E aprop senha sobre la arceria am tenta, e aprop inscideys quascuna am le spatum de quascuna partida agut am inscizio pervenient entro al os, e sia aquo per la latitut del cap.	And then take note on the artery with a probe, and then cut each one with the spatula of each part, sharp and incisive, entering into the bone, and this is so in the latitude of the head.
E si vols, entromet le spatum dejos la arteria e trenqua aquala a las inciden a las partidas desus.	And if you wish, insert the spatula below the artery and cut it where it meets the incisions in the parts above.
E sia la longitut de la inscizio cays dos ditz ajustatz, quar quan alcuna vena es inscizida le sanc es eyssit am egressio pulsatil, le qual saut deforo per saut frequent.	And let the length of the incision be about two inches, so that when some vein is cut, the blood flows out with a pulsating efflux, which springs forth frequently.
Mays si la arceria no apareys al cintiment, lahoras cove que tu mesures de la aurelha la quantitat del spazi de tres ditz, e aprop senha am tenta, e fen entro al os.	But if the artery does not appear at the incision, then it is good that you measure from the ear the quantity of space of three inches, and then take note with a probe, and enter into the bone.
E aquo que cove getar del sanc es quantitat de vi unc., e fort leu ne geta de lu mays o mens, e tot aquo es segon la quantitat la qual appareys de la vertut del malaute e de la replecio de la arceria de lu.	And as for how much blood to let out, it is about one pint. and not too little or too much, and all this is according to the quantity which appears of the virtue of the patient's disease and of the filling of the artery.
E aprop considera la plagua, e donc si reman sobre le os alcuna causa del ciphac, lahoras inscindys aquo per so que no endevengua apostema caut.	And then consider the wound, and therefore if there remains on the bone some cause of the skull, then cut away this part in order that the apostema may not become cauterized.
E aprop strenh la plagua am plumassols e am liamentz de drap de li, e aprop cura aquela am enguentz entro que sia sanat.	And then strengthen the wound with poultices and ligatures of linen cloth, and then cure it with unguents until it is healed.
Capitol .iii.	Chapter Three.
De extraccio de las arcerias las quals so en las templas.	On the Extraction of the Arteries which are in the Temples.
Quan ad alcu accideys emigranea antiqua o catertz agutz, per humiditatz agrimonials e per qualiditat en les lacertz des templas, o sodo antiqua vehement e semblantz ad aquels, e es medicat am las manieyras de curacio de medicina e aquo no comfereys, lahoras nos hem sproatz en aquestas malautias extraccio de las arcerias en les templas, o cauterizacio de aquelas ayssi cum havem mostrat.	When an ancient or recent emigration occurs in the temples, due to old and humid climates and qualities of the lacertae des temples, or a violent and ancient heat similar to those, and it is medicated with the methods of cure of medicine and this does not conform, then we have resorted to these diseases by extracting the arteries in the temples, or cauterizing them as we have shown.
E la manieyra de la operacio e extracio de aquelas es que·l malaute raza les pels les quals son en les templas; e entenda a la arceria apparent en le templar quar ela es a tu mostrada per le sieu pols, e·s occultada sino en paucs homes per vehemencia de freg.	And the manner of the operation and extraction of those is that the patient feels the pulse which are in the temples; and understand the artery which appears on the temple, for it is shown to you by its pulsation, and is hidden except in a few men by the vehemence of heat.
E si a tu es occultada, lahoras le col del malaute sia strengut am alcun drap; e aprop fregua le loc am un drap aspre o evapora le loc am aygua cauda entro que aparesca a tu la arceria manifestament.	And if it is hidden from you, then the patient's neck should be strengthened with some cloth; and then apply a rough cloth to the location or evaporate the location with hot water until the artery appears manifestly.
E lahoras tu pren le spatum del qual aquesta es la forma:	And then take the spatula, of which this is the form:
E aprop tu scorja la codena am aquel am facilitat entro que pervenguas a la arceria; e aprop geta en lu onti e extratz aquela a las partidas sobiranas entro que extraguas aquela de la codena e descobras aquela de las tunicas las quals so dejos aquela, de tota partida.	And then you should scrape the vertebra with that spatula with ease until you reach the artery; and then cut it at the point where it is bent and extract it from the upper parts until you remove it from the vertebra and discover those tunics which are below it, on all sides.
Mays si la arteria es subtil, lahoras envolveys aquela am la extremitat del oncii, e aprop inscindeys de aquela una partida segon la quantitat per la qual sian alonguadas las extremitatz de lu e sian contraytas, e no endevindra flux de sanc, quar si no so inscididas no pujara le sanc de tot.	But if the artery is subtle, then envelop it with the tip of the spatula, and then incise one part of it according to the quantity by which the ends of it are lengthened and contracted, and there will be no bleeding, for if they are not cut off, the blood will not flow at all.
E aprop evacua del sanc de vi unc. entro a tres.	And then evacuate about one pint of blood. until three pints.
E si la arceria es gran, lahoras cove que tu lies aquela en dos locs am fiel dopble fort de ceda o am cordas a lonc, e no coyte a lu putrefaccio denant la consolidacio de la plagua e endevengua flux de sanc.	And if the artery is great, then it is good that you divide it into two parts with a double ligature of thread or with cords at length, and do not allow it to putrefy before the wound has consolidated and bleeding has ceased.
E aprop incideys la superfluitat la qual es entre dos liamentz; e fay aquo en aquela hora o aprop autra ora.	And then cut away the superfluity which is between two ligatures; and do this at that hour or shortly after.
E si vols, cauteriza aquela am cauteri entro al os am cauteri cutellar entro que sian incididas las extramitatz de lu, e stara en loc de aquela meteyssa obra.	And if you wish, cauterize that part with a cauterizer into the bone and with a cutlery cauterizer until the ends of it are cut off, and remain in place for that medley of work.
E es milhor obra sino que·l malaute aia febre o es de escalfada compleccio; quar cauteri es de aquelas causas que ajudan a las humiditatz finidoras, e donc es milhor en juvament.	And it is better work if the patient has fever or is of a warm complexion; for cauterization is one of those causes that help to end humidity, and therefore it is better in youth.
E cove aprop la extraccio de las arcerias que huomplas le loc de coto antic, e sian pausatz sobre lu polvils decentement fayt, e aprop sia curat am medicinas seccas fazen naysser la carn e am calguas entro que sia sanat.	And it is good to apply the extraction of arteries which fills the old wound, and be placed on the powder decently made, and then be cured with dry medicines that make the flesh appear and with some ointment until it is healed.
E si mentre obres autra veguada endeventa flux de sanc de la arceria, lahora tu te coyta a restrenger aquel sanc, o am cauteri, o que omplas le loc de coto, e strenh la tua ma entro que sia restreyt le sanc.	And if while you are working another time blood flows from the artery, then immediately stop that bleeding with a ligature, or with a cauterizer, or by filling the wound with a cloth, and strengthen your hand until the bleeding is stopped.
E si deguna causa de aquelas no es a tu present, lahoras pausa le tieu dit sobre le loc entro que·l sanc sia congilat, e enbroca le loc am aygua de vehement fregiditat entro que la acuitat repausa, e sia strengut segon que cove.	And if no cause of those is present with you, then pause your hand on the location until the blood has coagulated, and envelop the location with hot water of vehement warmth, so that the sharpness may be stilled, and strengthen as needed.
E aquo que es pus leugier en extraccio de arceria es que tu cauterizes la vena am aquest cauteri haventz dos cotels, pus que tu has senhat les dos locs am tenta, e depausa quascus, mot ignitz, entro que pervenguan al os e inscindan la vena en dos locs, per so que sia elonguat aquo que es entre las extremitatz de lu, quar no son consolidadas de tot am aquest cauteri.	And that which is easier in the extraction of arteries is that you cauterize the vein with this cauterizer having two sheaths, since you have marked the two locations with a probe, and then deposit each one, quietly, until they reach the bone and cut the vein in two places, so that what is between the ends of it may be lengthened, for they are not fully consolidated by this cauterization.
E aquesta es la forma del cauteri:	And this is the form of the cauterizer:
E sia la acuitat dels dos cotels esemps.	And the sharpness of the two sheaths are examples.
Mays empero si so mendres acuitat que dos cotels es milhor, quar si so agudas cum dos cotels propera a quascuna freg, e no enscideysso la carn am velocitat.	But rather if the sharpness is less than two sheaths, it is better, for if they are sharp like two sheaths, close to each other, and do not cut into the flesh with velocity.
Donc cum en aquels es alcuna grossitut, es tenguda la calor del foc en aquels e la carn es abscindida leugierament.	Therefore, as in those there is some thickness, the heat of the fire is kept in them and the flesh is cut away slightly.
E aquesta obra es milhor en tota obra e pus leugiera.	And this work is better than all other works and more gentle.
E sia le spazi le qual es entre dos cotels la quantitat de la grossesa del dit.	And the space which is between two sheaths is the quantity of thickness of that digit.
Capitol quart.	Chapter Four.
De la cura de cors de lagremas agudas e aciduas dels huels.	On the Cure of Eyes with Acute and Acid Tears.
Quan so lagremas aciduas, e es le cors de aquelas venas las quals so sobre le test del cap deforo, e no comfereys en aquo alcuna causa de la curacio de medicina, e vezes la cara del malaute ja enrogesir e sent en le sieu front deambulacio ayssi cum si era deambulacio de formiguas, e·ls huels de aquel so extenuatz, humitz enayssi que ja les pels de lor son conodutz, e las parpelas so scalfadas per la acuitat de las lacrimas, les antics agro mesties en la curacio de aquelas de aquesta operacio, e nompnero aquela curacio am spassa.	When the tears are acidic, and the body of those veins which are above the forehead is affected outside, and there is no conformity in this with any cause of medicine, and the face of the patient becomes reddened and he feels a wandering movement in his own forehead, as if it were a migration of ants, and the eyes of that person are exhausted, humidified to such an extent that their lids have become constricted, and the eyelids are scorched by the acidity of the tears, the ancient physicians used to mix certain medicines for this cure, and they called that cure "spassa".
E es que tu comandas al malaute rayre les pels les quals son en le sieu front, e aprop inscideys en le front tres fissuras engualment distans segon la longitut del front.	And it is that you command the patient to scratch the skin which is on his forehead, and then cut three incisions equally distant from each other according to the length of the forehead.
E si’ la longitut de la fissura cays dos ditz: la una fissura sia engualment distant a la longitut del nas en le mieg loc del front, e la segonda segon la longitut un petit del movement dels lacertz les quals so en le lacrimal, e la tersa del autre part.	And if the length of the incision is about two inches: one incision shall be equally distant from the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second according to the length of a little movement of the lacertae which are in the lacrimal, and the third on the other side.
E guarda te de la incizio de las arcerias las quals so en dos latz, e elongua la tua ma de la continuacio de amdos las mandibulas.	And beware of the cutting of the arteries which are in two sides, and lengthen your hand with the continuation of both jawbones.
E si’ l’espazi de quascuna inscizio la quantitat de tres ditz ajustatz.	And if the space of each incision is about three inches adjusted.
E si’ a tu una pessa d’espongua apparelhada o draps seccatz motz am les quals exsiccas le sanc.	And if you have a piece of sponge appareled or dry cloths, moderately moistened with which you can absorb the blood.
E aprop entremet le spatum de dos agudas extremitatz, del qual aquesta es la forma de la inscisio de lu:	And then insert the spatula of two sharp ends, the form of which is as follows:
que es de la partida des templas entro a la segonda inscizio.	which is from the temple to the second incision.
Exxcorja am aquel tota la codena la qual es entre dos incizios am le ciphac le qual es sobre le os, e aprop fay aquo de la inscizio migera entro a la segonda inscisio.	Excise the entire cord which is between two incisions on the skullbone above the bone, and then make this way from the first incision to the second.
E aprop stratz ne aquest spatum e entromet en la primieyra inscizio autra vetz un autre instrument le qual es apelat cutellar, agut de una part e del autre no agut.	And then strengthen the spatula and insert it into the first incision another time with a different instrument which is called a cutellar, sharp on one side and not sharp on the other.
E pausa le latz de aquel agut deves la carn annexa deves la codena, e le latz de lu leon dintz le os, e empelley aquel entro que pervengua a la fissura migera, e abscindeys am aquel totz les vaysels que descendo del cap als huels.	And pause the edge of that instrument so that it cuts through the flesh and cord, and then insert it into the bone so that it reaches the middle incision, and cut away with it all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes.
Mays que sia continuada la inscizio ad aquo appar de la codena, e aprop fay aquo en la fissura migana entro al autra fissura.	But then continue the incision up to where the cord appears, and then make it so in the middle incision into the other incision.
E pus que corr del sanc quantitat engual, exprem les locs de las pessas del sanc congilat.	And when a quantity of blood equal to that amount is released, press the places where the coagulated blood has collected.
E aprop pausa en quascuna fissura calgua de coto vielh, e pausa sobre aquels polvils enbegutz en vi e oli e vi agre, e vegas que no endevengua apostema caut.	And then pause in each incision, allowing the cut to close like a old wound, and pause over those powders impregnated with vinegar and oil and vinegar, so that no cauterized apostema may appear.
E en le tertz dia deslia le liament e aministra gran enfusio de aygua cauda o tebeza, e aprop cura aquo am enguent bazilicon am oli rozat e autres entro que las plaguas sian sanadas.	And on the third day, untie the ligature and administer a great abundance of hot water or tea, and then cure it with an ointment of basilicum and rose oil and others until the wounds are healed.
Capitol .v.	Chapter Five.
De la cura de lagramas per catartz e als huels descendentz de las partidas dedintz del cap.	On the Cure of Tears through Catarrh and descending to the eyes from the partitions behind the head.
Quan ad alcu veno catartz agutz e continuantz, e vezes les huels del malaute extenuatz petitz, e ja le reguardament de lor es debelitat, e las palpebras ulceradas e de lor cazo les pels, e en le preon del cap es dolor aguda ledent e extrenutacio consequent, lahoras sapias per aquestz accidentz que las materias e catartz no veno sino de motas venas de las partidas dedintz procedent.	When there is acute catarrh and continued flowing, and the patient's eyes are exhausted and small, and their gaze is weakened, and the eyelids are ulcerated and their skin is raw, and in the forehead of the head there is a sharp pain and subsequent exhaustion, then you should know through these accidents that the matters and catarrh come from many veins proceeding from behind.
E la milhor curacio en aquels es aquesta: que comandes al malaute que raza lo sieu front, e aprop inscideys en aquel una fissura al mieg loc del front, un petit per la latitut (e comensa am la fissura del templar senestre entro al dextre templar; e sia inscisio entro al os; e eslongua la tua ma dels lacertz del templas lesquals son maugutz deves la mastigacio), entro que sia le os descubert.	And the best cure for those is this: that you command the patient to scratch his forehead, and then cut a incision in the middle of the forehead, a little distance apart (and it begins with the incision of the left temple to the right temple; and be an incision into the bone; and lengthen your hand from the lacertae of the temples which are most suitable for mastigacio), until the bone is revealed.
Exsicca tot le sanc am espongua o am drap secc e aprop repleys entre las doas labias de la fissura am coto vielh o am draps de li.	Dry out all the blood with sponge or dry cloth and then fill it between the two lips of the incision with an old wound or with cloths tied.
E aprop estrenh desus am polvils enbegutz en vi e oli per so que no endevengua apostema caut.	And then strengthen above with powders impregnated with vinegar and oil, so that no cauterized apostema may appear.
E quan deslias aquo e veses que l’apostema ja es diminuit, lahoras cove que fregua le os entro que comensa en lu nayser carn, e aprop cura aquel am regiment exsiccatiu le qual fassa neysser la carn, ayssi cum si tu prenes de farina de froment dos partidas e de colofania quatre partidas e mescla o, e de lor sia fayt emplastre e sia aministrat en aquestas plaguas a de la carn nativitat.	And when you see that the apostema has diminished, then it is good to apply heat to the bone until it begins to produce flesh, and then cure it with an exsicative regimen which makes the flesh appear, just as if you take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophonium, and mix them together, and from that make a poultice and administer it to these wounds for the nativity of the flesh.
Capitol .vi.	Chapter Six.
De la cura de aquo que catz en las aurelhas.	On the Cure of that which Catarrhs in the Ears.
Tota causa que catz en las aurelhas es una de quatre specias, quar o es peyra mineral o causa semblant a peyra, ayssi cum ferr e veyre, o es de planta ayssi cum ceze o fava, o es causa fluxtibla ayssi cum aygua e vi agre e a lor semblantz, o alcuna bestia.	All causes that catarrh in the ears are one of four species, for it is either mineral pyre or a similar cause like iron and vinegar, or it is from plants like cheese or fava, or it is a fluxible cause like hot water and vinegar and their likenesses, or some animal.
E donc quan peyra catz en l’aurelha o autra causa semblant de aquelas causas que no ajustan ne creysso en l’aurelha, e pausa la aurelha al solelh, e si vezes la peyra, lahoras distilla en aquela alcuna causa de oli violat o sizami, e aprop aministra la extraccio de lu, e fay le stornudar am condizi, e oppila las nars deve le aveniment de stornutacio.	And therefore when pyre catarrh in the ear or another similar cause from those causes that do not adjust nor believe in the ear, and pause the ear at the sun, and if times the pyre, then it is good to distill some cause of violet oil or size, and then administer the extraction of it, and make the nose run with conditions, and stop up the nostrils by the happening of sneezing.
E aprop pausa en le circuit de la aurelha alscunas pessas de drap o lana, e dextendas la aurelha a las partidas desus, quar motas veguadas es foro-getada am aquestas causas.	And then pause in the circuit of the ear some pieces of cloth or wool, and stretch the ear to the upper parts, for many times it is forgotten with these causes.
E si no n’es getada, lahoras aministra extraccio de lu am le instrument apelat gesti epicicarios subtil del qual aquesta es la forma:	And if it is not gotten, then it is good to administer the extraction of it with the instrument called "epicicario" which has a subtle shape.
E si es foro-getada am gesti, bo es; e sino, lahoras aministra la extraccio de lu am onci subtil de pauca duplicacio.	And if it is forgotten with the instrument, then it is good; and otherwise, it is good to administer the extraction of it with a subtle bone of slight duplication.
E donc si no es foro-getada per aquo, lahoras fay una canula de aram e entromet la extremitat de la canula en le trauc de la aurelha e claus a l’enviro de la canula am cera e am oli mollificada per so que no sia ubert sino la canula.	And therefore if it is not forgotten for this, then it is good to make a needle of iron and insert the tip of the needle into the ear canal and close around the needle with wax and softened oil so that only the needle remains.
E aprop extratz am le tieu vent am fort atraccio, quar tropas veguadas cum aquo que havem recontat.	And then extract with your breath a strong attraction, for many times as we have recounted.
Mays si no es foro-getada en aquesta manieyra, lahoras pren de halka alumbat o de vecz aparelhat am le qual son preses les ausels una patita quantitat, e pausa aquel en la extremitat de ray, e aprop envolopa sobre aquel coto decentment pausat.	But if it is not forgotten in this manner, then it is good to take a piece of burnt bark or a prepared wickerwork with which the birds are caught and having taken a small quantity, place it at the end of the ray, and then wrap around it decently placed.
E aprop entromet aquel en le trauc de la aurelha am facilitat, e aprop excicca la aurelha de la humiditat.	And then insert that into the ear canal with ease, and then dry out the ear of its humidity.
E donc si no es foro-getada am totas las causas las quals havem recontadas, lahoras tu coyta a talhar aquela denant que endevengua apostema caut o espasme.	And therefore if it is not forgotten with all the causes that we have recounted, then you should stop cutting before it becomes cauterized or spasmed.
E la manieyra de talhar aquela es que tu al comensament sancnes le malaute de la vena sephasica e extratz del sanc segon la mannieyra de la vertut de lu, e aprop fay aquel cezer entre las tuas mas e converteys l’aurelha a las partidas desus, e fen am petita fissura en la razit de la aurelha deves lo greys de lu en le loc be premegut de lu.	And the manner of cutting is that you first bleed the patient from the saphenous vein and extract the blood according to the virtue of it, and then make it cease between your hands and convert the ear into the upper parts, and finally make a small incision in the root of the ear just above the grey hairs of it.
E sia la fissura de figura lunar entro que pervengua a la peyra, e, la peyra atrobada, osta aquela si podes am instrumentz apropriatz; e aprop cos la fissura en aquela hora am velocitat, e cura aquela entro que sia sanat.	And then make the incision of lunar shape until it reaches the pyre, and when the pyre is blackened, stop that if you can with proper instruments; and then close the incision in that hour with speed, and cure it so that it may be healed.
E si la causa cazent en la aurelha es un dels gras que creysso e so inflatz, lahoras aministra la curacio e la extraccio de lu; mays si no obezeys a tu ad eyssiment, lahoras tu pren spatum teune subtil segon aquesta forma:	And if the cause that catarrhs in the ear is one of those fats that believe and are inflated, then it is good to administer the cure and extraction of it; but if it does not obey your attention, then you should take a spatula of fine steel according to this form:
e aministra am aquel la abscizio de aquel gra lo qual es cazut en l’aurelha.	and administer with that the removal of that fat which is catarrhs in the ear.
E no fassas aquo quan cogitas que aquel ja es humectat per la vapor del aurelha, e pausa aquel en motas pessas, e prop extratz ne aquelas am les oncis o am gesti subtil, o ab inscizio ayssi co dit havem, quar es alleujada la extraccio de lu.	And do not do this when you think that it is already moistened by the vapor of the ear, and pause it in many pieces, and then extract from those with the onces or subtle gestures, or with incision as we have said, for it is alleviated the extraction of it.
Mays en l’aygua la qual es intrada en l’aurelha cove que·l malaute use de sternutacio am condizi al comensament, e omple la sieua aurelha am alcu coto vielh, e jagua sobre aquela aurelha en la qual es l’aygua, e si per aquo es foro-getada, bo es; e sino, lahoras pren tropas peyras teunas e leons segon la longitut del dit, e calfa aquelas en le foc un pauc, e le pacient entrometa una de aquelas en le trauc de la sua aurelha e saute sobre la un pe sieu de aquela partida e percussia am una autra peyra sobre la peyra la qual es dintz la aurelha.	But in the water which is entered into the ear, it is good for the patient to use sneezing with conditions at first, and fill his own ear with a little old cloth, and then pour over that ear where there is water, and if by this it is forgotten, it is good; otherwise, you should take many hot irons and lemons according to the length of the digit, and burn those in the fire for a while, and have the patient insert one of those into his own ear canal and beat with another iron on the iron which is behind the ear.
Donc no cesse aquo am peyra entro que tota l’aygua sia foro-getada.	So do not cease doing this with pyre until all the water is forgotten.
E ja l’aygua sira foro-getada enayssi que tu prenguas de papier o de gonc .i., e met la una extremetat de lu en l’aurelha e estendas l’autre extremitat am foc entro que sia comburit le may de lu.	And then the water will be forgotten in such a way that you take from paper or cotton gauze. and put one end of it into the ear and stretch the other end with fire until the tip of it is burned.
E prop met i autre gonc e fay aquo tantas veguadas entro que tota l’aygua sia foro-getada, e stratz aquel am canula ayssi co desus es dit de la peyra extrasadora.	And then put in another gauze and make it so many times until all the water is forgotten, and stretch that with a needle as described above of the extracting pyre.
Mays en la extraccio de bestia intrant en aquela aurelha, si es a petit cos, ayssi piussa e a lu semblant, cura aquel ayssi cum havem dit en la divisio; mays si es de gran cos la qual causa apar al sen del vezement, lahoras aministra la extraccio de lu am gesti e oncis, e la causa de lu es pus leugiera de totas las autras causas que cazo en l’aurelha.	But in the extraction of beast that enters into that ear, if it is small, thus push and pull similar to the sound, cure that as we have said in the division; but if it is from a great body which appears on the side of the vessel, then it is good to administer the extraction of it with gestures and onces, and the cause of it is less severe than all the other causes that catarrhs in the ear.
Mays en la extraccio de verm engendrat en la aurelha, quan tu curas aquel am aquo que havem dit en la divisio e en le tractat de distillacios e no comfereys la tua curacio, lahoras cove que tu reguardes la aurelha al solelh.	But in the extraction of worm generated in the ear, when you cure that with the water that we have said in the division and in the treatise on distillations and do not confirm your cure, then it is good to look at the ear towards the sun.
E donc si apar aqui alcuna causa dels verms, lahoras extratz aquel am gesti o am onci subtils, mays si no apar deguna causa, lahoras pren una canula dejos streyta e desus ampla de la qual aquesta es la forma de lu:	And therefore if any cause of worms appears here, then you should extract that with gestures or subtle onces; but if no cause appears, then you should take a needle that is straight and wide from which this is the form:
E entromet la extremitat subtil en la aurelha segon la quantitat la qual suffertar puesca le malaute; e aprop sucgeys am aquela per succio fort, e fay aquo motas veguadas, entro que totz les verms sian foro-gitatz.	And insert the subtle tip into the ear according to the quantity which can be borne by the patient; and then suck it out with a strong suction, and make this many times, until all the worms are forgotten.
Mays si no obezeysso a tu al ayssiment, lahoras tu opila e claus en le circuit de la canula am cera ayssi cum havem dit; lahoras aministre distillacios las quals han ja esproadas les antics en la curacio dels verms, e atrobaras aquo en le tractat de distillacios.	But if it does not obey your attention, then you should stop and close the circuit of the needle with wax as we have said; and then administer distillations which have already been tried by the ancients in the cure of worms, and find this in the treatise on distillations.
E sia la tua efusio am la qual efundas les olis medicinas en la aurelha am aquest strument del qual aquesta es la forma de lu:	And then your effusion with which you pour the medicinal oils into the ear with this instrument of which this is the form:
E fay aquela de argent o de eram, dejos streyt, en le qual sia un petit trauc, e am pla desus.	And make that of silver or of iron, straight, with a small hole, and on top.
E donc sia cum empellent a que es en la conquavitat de la canula de continent aqui on sira necessari.	And therefore so it is when you need to extract what is in the cavity of the needle's continuation here where it will be necessary.
E si vols, pren le ray e envolveys en la extremitat de lu decentment coto, e aprop gieta oli en la concavitat del auziment, o suc de alcuna herba, o aquo que vols de aquestas medicinas en la canula — e aquela es en la aurelha —, e aprop entromet le ray am coto desus e exprem am la tua ma aquel am compressio temprada de lu entro que l’oli sia expellit en la concavitat del auziment e le malaute senta le oli dedintz.	And if you wish, take the thread and wrap it around the tip of the needle decently and tightly, and then pour oil into the cavity of the ascending, or juice from some herb, or whatever you want from these medicines in the needle — and that is in the ear —, and then insert the thread with a knot above and express with your hand that on gentle compression of it so that the oil is expelled into the cavity of the ascending and the patient feels the oil outside.
E aquo que sia enfundut en la aurelha sia ja scalfat am foc un petit.	And what is inserted into the ear is already scorched with fire for a little while.
E guarda te que la causa la qual distillaras en l’aurelha no sia trop frega, quar las medicinas de aurelha no suffertan aquo.	And be careful that the cause which you will distill into the ear is not too hot, for the medicines of the ear do not tolerate this.
Capitol .vii.	Chapter VII.
De curacio de opilacio de aurelhas.	On the Cure of Ear Plugging.
Alcunas veguadas alcus enfantz yeysso dels ventres de lors mayres no-perforatz, e aquo ja accideys en alcus homes, opilacio en le meat de la aurelha per plagua o per carn nada en aquela; e aquesta opilacio alcunas veguadas es fayta en le preon del trau de la aurelha la qual no consiec le vezement, e alcunas veguadas es en las partidas defora.	Some times some children or even adults have a blockage in the ear canal due to a wound or flesh that is not perforated; and this blockage sometimes occurs in the inner ear or in the outer parts.
E aquela que accideys en le preon de lu, la qual no comprehen le vezement, es en las majors disposicios de dificil sanacio.	And that which occurs in the inner part of it, which does not comprehend the vessel, is in the greatest difficulties for difficult healing.
E en aquela en qual consegueys le vezement, cove que tu pauses la aurelha del malaute al solelh e reguarda en aquela.	And in that which you succeed in comprehending the vessel, it is good to pause the ear of the patient in the sun and look at it.
E donc si vezes oppulacio apparent, obre aquela am espatum subtil del qual aquesta es la forma de lu:	And therefore if you see obvious opilation, open that with a fine spatula of which this is the form:
Si’ la extremitat de lu en la qual sia petita la latitut, del qual la una partida sia aguda e l’autra no; e le spatum sia de dos latz leon per so que no fassa lizio al aurelha.	If the tip of it is in the ear canal where there is a small distance, with one side being sharp and the other not; and the spatula has two lion-shaped sides so that it does not cause irritation to the ear.
E donc si la opilacio es per carn nascuda en la aurelha o en le meat de lu, lahoras te aquela am oncis subtils e incidiys aquela vehement facilitat entro que sia ostada tota la carn.	And therefore if the blockage is due to flesh born in the ear or in the ear canal, then you should cut it with subtle onces and incise that with great ease until all the flesh is removed.
E si opilacio es en le preon de la aurelha, lahoras pren ray subtil leon e escalfa aquel am foc un pauc, e aprop met aquel en le meat de l’aurelha.	And if the blockage is in the inner part of the ear, then you should take a subtle thread of lion and heat it with fire for a little while, and then insert that into the ear canal.
E donc si as scentit oppulacio am aquo que le malaute atroba am facilitat, per gravetat de ausir, esforsa la oppressio de lu am facilitat; e guarda te que no plagues les nervis del aurelha.	And therefore if you have sensed blockage with that which the patient experiences with ease, due to the weight of having heard, try to relieve the oppression of it with ease; and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear.
E aprop pausa en l’aurelha drap de li segon la quantitat del ample del trauc lo qual tu as envolvutz en l’enguent egipciac; e fay aquo per alcus jorns entro que sias segur de la consolidacio de la plagua; o que prenguas qualgua e enfon aquela en ayguaros e pulveriza sobre lu segi trissat e usa de lu; e si vezes la aurelha ja esser apostemada, lahoras cove que tu estraguas la qualgua e permutes aquela am autra qualgua la qual tu envoloparas en cerot que sia fayt am oli rozat, entro que sia le apostema caut cedat; e aprop cura aquel entro que sia sanat.	And then pause in the ear with cloth of linen according to the quantity of the width of the canal which you have wrapped with Egyptian ointment; and make this for several days until you are sure of the consolidation of the wound; or take some vinegar and soak it in water and powderize over it, and use it; and if the ear is already cauterized, then it is good to remove the vinegar and replace it with another vinegar which you have wrapped in wax that is made with rose oil, until the cauterized apostema yields; and then cure that until it is healed.
Mays si accideys flux de sanc, lahoras submergeys esponga o drap en aygua frega e pausa sobre la aurelha, e usa del autra curacio la qual restrengeys le flux del sanc, la qual es dita en le tractat de distillacio.	But if there is bleeding, then submerge a sponge or cloth in hot water and pause it over the ear, and use another cure which restricts the flow of blood, as described in the treatise on distillation.
Capitol .viii.	Chapter VIII.
De cura de athezil le qual endeveno a las palpebras.	On the Cure of Athazil which affects the Eyelids.
Athezil les quals endeveno a las paupebras dels huels alcuna veguada so humitz, alscunas veguadas son secs.	Athazils which affect the eyelids of humans sometimes become moist, and at other times they are dry.
Donc cove que tu tenguas aquels am tenhalhas o am onci, e inscindas aquels am espatum de las suas razitz, e aprop pausa sobre les locs segi trissat.	Therefore it is good that you take those with needles or onces, and incise them with an instrument from their roots, and then pause over the places as described.
Mays si dolor am flux de sanc veno, lahoras tu cauteriza aquels am cauteri lanticular subtil.	But if pain and bleeding come, then you should cauterize those with a thin lunar cauterizer.
E la milhor cauterizacio es aprop las inscizios e tropas veguadas retornam quan reman alcuna causa de sas razitz; e quan so cauterizadas am foc, aquelas razitz son comburidas e no retornan.	And the best cauterization is when you insert it into the incisions and many times return, as long as there remains some cause of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
Capitol .ix.	Chapter IX.
Cura de grandeyssa que veno a las palpebras dels huels.	Cure of Grandeyssa which comes to the Eyelids of Humans.
Motas veguadas endeve en las palpebras dels huels alcuna causa la qual es asemblada a grandissa en sa fortalicia e duricia, e per so grandissia es apelada.	Many times it grows on the eyelids of humans some cause which is assembled with grandeyssa in its strength and hardness, and therefore grandeyssa is called.
E es agreguacio de humiditat grossa en la palpebra dejos e desus.	And it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the eyelid below and above.
Donc la opperacio en lor es que consideras lahoras si la grandissia es procedent en lu en aquo que apar de la palpebra e es mauguda a tota partida; e la causa de lu es leugiera.	Therefore the operation on them is that you consider whether the grandeyssa is proceeding from there in what appears from the eyelid and is spread to all parts; and the cause of it is light.
Donc fen sobre aquela am fissura per la latitut, e aprop escorga aquela de tota partida am facilitat entro que evasesca, e aprop suspen aquela am onci e abscindeys aquela.	Therefore proceed with an incision by the distance, and then search out that part from all parts with ease until it evacuates, and then suspend that with a needle and excise it.
Mays si a tu no es apparelhada la incizio de lu si no pus que penetras la palpebra am inscizio pauc a pauc, lahoras aquo no notz en deguna causa.	But if you are not skilled in the incision of it and only push to penetrate the eyelid with a slight incision by degrees, then this is not noted in any cause.
E si la figura es gran, lahoras tu l’ajusta am sutura; e cura aquela entro que sia sanada.	And if the figure is great, then you should adjust it with a suture; and cure that until it is healed.
E si es pauca, a tu no sobrevindra mal per aquela quar l’anguent de lu restaura aquela e encarna.	And if it is slight, you will not suffer harm from it, because the ointment of it restores that and fleshens.
E si la grandissia es declinant a las partidas dedintz de la palpebra deves la superficia dedintz, lahoras evesa la palpebra e suspen la grandissia am onci, otra que tu indigescas de incizio, e prem aquela de tota part, e si la palpebra per inscizio es alonguada, aquo no notz en deguna causa.	And if the grandeyssa is declining to the outer parts of the eyelid, then you should smooth out the surface outwardly; and then elevate the eyelid and suspend the grandeyssa with a needle, unless you need an incision, and press that from all parts; and if the eyelid by incision is lengthened, this is not noted in any cause.
E aprop la incizio, lava le huel am aygua salada; e cura le loc am aquo que encarna entro que sia sanat.	And then, with the incision, wash the eyes with salt water; and cure the place with that which fleshens until it is healed.
Capitol .x.	Chapter X.
De la cura axcirnah en la palpebra desus del huel.	On the Cure of Axirnah in the Eyelid above the Eye.
Axcirnath es grays le qual es engendrat en las tunicas de la palpebra desus, e majorment endeve als enfantz, agrava les huels de aquels et accideyso a lor catartz le mayti; e no podon reguardar la claror del solelh per aquo quar lagremas se coytan ad aquels.	Axcirnah is a grayish thing which is generated in the tunics of the eyelid above, and mainly affects children, aggravates their eyes, and causes great harm to them; and they cannot gaze at the brightness of the sun because of it, so that tears are shed upon them.
E per so tu vezes aquels jaser sobre les lors caras tot temps, e sobre les lors caras dormen; e so a las palpebras de lor dejos les sobrecils humidas, las quals ja ha cuberta imflacio, e iminencia de accernac apparent es en l’uelh; e que quant tu premes le loc am les tieus ditz, tu centes accernac entro aquels.	And so you will have them weep constantly on their faces, and sleep on their faces; and thus the eyelids of theirs below are overcast with moistened lids, which already has swelling, and apparent danger is in the eye; and when you press the place with those words, you will cause harm within them.
E alcuna manieyra de opperacio es en aquel que le malaute pausa le sieu cap en le tieu se, e aprop pausa drap de li e de lu fay calgua, e fay de lu cercle segon la quantitat la qual contena arthernach de tota partida, e aprop pausa aquel sobre aquela e prem am les tieus ditz de tota per que sia agreguat arcernac en le mieg del cercle, e aprop fen en le mieg de aquela humiditat am spatum inscident am fissura per la latitut, e la fissura no sia major que la fissura que es fayta en flaubotomia.	And one manner of operation is that the patient places their own head on the bed, and then pauses a cloth of linen and of water to make a poultice, and makes from it a circle according to the quantity which contains arthernach from all parts; and then pauses that over that and presses with the words of totality so that harm is aggregated in the middle of the circle; and then proceeds in the middle of that moisture with an instrument inserted into a slit by the distance, and the slit should not be greater than the slit made in flabotomia.
Mays en le preon cove que tu fendas la codena tota entro que pervenguas ad arcernach, quar en las mays desposicios proceseys arcernach per fissura segon la forma de grayseza blanca.	But in the forefront it is good that you cut the cord entire until you reach arthernach, for in the greatest dispositions, arthernach proceeds by slit according to the form of white greasiness.
Donc extratz aquela am draps los quals tu as envolopatz entre les tieus ditz a las partidas deforo e revolv entre la ma dextra e sinistre entro que sia dispargut.	Therefore extract that with cloths which you have wrapped between the words of totality to the outer parts, and revolve between your right and left hand until it is scattered.
E guarda te que no ajustes en la fissura per so que am le spatum no pervenguas al huel e ladescas aquel.	And be careful not to insert in the slit because you may reach the eye with the instrument and damage that.
Mays si no apar a tu arternach en le comensament de la fissura, mays que tu ajustes en la fissura un petit am fecilitat entro que procesisca arternach; e aprop extratz aquela ayssi quo havem dit; e aprop submargeys draps de li en aygua e vi agre e pausa les sobre le loc e estrenh aquels am polvils.	But if there is no arthernach at the beginning of the slit, then adjust the slit a little with ease so that arthernach may proceed; and then extract that as we have said; and then submerge cloths in water, vinegar, and salt, and pause them over the place and strengthen those with powders.
E so alcus que trissan sal e pausan aquel en la conquavitat de la fissura per so que aquo que es remas de aquela humiditat.	And then some that trickle salt and pause it in the cavity of the slit, because this which remains of that humidity.
E aprop cura aquel entro que sia sanat.	And then cure that until it is healed.
Mays si accideys en le loc apostema caut, lahoras cura aquel am emplastres cedatils entro que sia sanat.	But if there is a cauterized apostema in the place, then cure that with soft poultices until it is healed.
Capitol .xi.	Chapter XI.
De manieyras de tactimi del huel.	On Manners of Touching the Eye.
Quan en las palpebras dels huels so natz pels ajustatz dejos les pels naturals e so antiquatz, lahoras aquels noso al huel e fan endevenir manieras de malautias ayssi cum lacrimas assiduas e mollificacio de palpebras e tela entro que aquo sia causa de destruccio del huel que s’apela tactinir del huel, e cura se en quatre manieyras: o per cauteri am foc; o am medicina acuta segon que denant es dit en le capitol de cauteri; o es fayt atactini per inscizio e sutura; o per cannas segon que yeu diyre.	When in the eyelids of humans there are knots, you should adjust those below with natural skin and thus make them old, then those above do not touch the eye and cause habits of illnesses such as constant tears and softening of eyelids and flesh until this becomes a cause of destruction of the eye which is called touching the eye, and cure it in four ways: or by cauterization with fire; or with sharp medicine according to what was said before in the chapter on cauterization; or by making an incision and suture; or through canals as I will say.
E donc cove que tu pauses le cap del malaute en le tieu se; aprop converteys la palpebra del uelh am la tua ma sinistra, e si es convertida, bo es; e sino, entromet agulha en aquela en la qual sia fiel de la partida pus dejos de la palpebra, e fay penetrar la agulha am fiel desus, e aquo sia — prop del marge de la palpebra en le qual naysso les pels — prop dels pels, e tira le fiel a las partidas desus am la palpebra, e converteys aquela am le ray.	And therefore it is good that you pause the head of the patient on the bed; then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand, and if it has turned, well it is; and otherwise, insert a needle into that in which there is a fold of the part more below than the eyelid, and make the needle penetrate through the fold above, and thus be - near the edge of the eyelid where there are hairs - next to the hairs, and pull the thread up to the parts above with the eyelid, and turn it with the thread.
E aprop fen en la partida dedintz de la palpebra dejos les pels ajustatz am spatum inscidentz del lacrimal major entro al lacrimal mendre; e aprop extratz le fiel e pausa dejos la palpebra polvilhs petitz de coto o de drap, e aprop senha sobre la palpebra am tenta, e sia ayssi cum figura de fuelha de mirt.	And then proceed in the outer part of the eyelid below the hairs adjusted with an instrument inserted into the lacrimal major canal until the lacrimal gland; and then extract the thread and pause below the eyelid with small powders of cotton or cloth, and then sign over the eyelid with a tent, and be like a figure of mirt leaves.
Mays empero cove que sia la figura segon la quantitat de helevacio de la palpebra, quar aquo ja es diversificat en les homes, quar de aquels es le quals indigeys que sia inscidit de la palpebra gran quantitat segon la quantitat per la qual la palpebra es mollificada.	But meanwhile it is good that the figure should be according to the quantity of swelling of the eyelid, for this already varies among men, because some of them need to have a great amount incised from the eyelid in proportion to the amount by which the eyelid is softened.
E aprop fen am le spatum sobre las doas linhas las quals has senhadas, e comensa del lacrimal major entro al lacrimal menor.	And then proceed with the instrument over the two lines which you have marked, and begin from the lacrimal major canal into the lacrimal minor canal.
E si’ la tua fissura prop dels pels naturals ayssi cum es la grossetut del rey.	And if your slit is as wide as the natural hairs, like it is the greatest thickness of a king.
E aprop met le onci en un dels dos angles de la codena, e aprop excoria aquela tota, e aprop ajusta am la scitura las doas labias am gula o fiel de lana subtil, e abstergeys le sanc, e fay adherir aquo que superflueys dels fiels sobre dos sobrecils am alcunas causas enviscans, si voles far aquo, e sino, non cures.	And then put the needle in one of the two angles of the cord, and then excise it entirely, and then adjust with a suture the two lips with a subtle gullet or thread, and cleanse the wound, and make adhere what superfluous threads there are on top of two eyelids with some causes visible; if you want to do so, and otherwise, do not cure.
E aprop leyssa la sutura dels fiels entro a tres dias o quatre, e aprop cura aquo.	And then loosen the suture of the threads within three or four days, and then cure that.
E si vols, layssa la plagua ses sutura, e cura aquela am aquo que exsicca e constrenh, quar la palpebra es alevada deves la sigillacio de la plagua e la agreguacio de lu; mays sutura es milor E donc aysso diysso les antics de taxanir.	And if you wish, leave the wound without suture and cure it with that which dries and tightens, for the eyelid is raised by the sealing of the wound and the accumulation of fluid; but suture is better. Therefore thus I say to those who are old in taxinir.
Mays empero en lu sia sollicitut sobre le malaute, e es de bona operacio, e no es en lu temor.	But meanwhile on him there is solicitude for the patient, and it is of good operation, and not in his fear.
E es autra manieyra en taxmir, e es que senhes sobre la palpebra figura ayssi cum fuelha de mirt, e aprop eleva la palpebra am tres uncis segreguatz e congreguatz segon aquesta forma:	And there is another manner in taxinir, and it is that you mark on the eyelid a figure like mirt leaves, and then raise the eyelid with three threads separated and gathered according to this form:
Mays si no es possible aquo, tener les uncis, e aquo no es engualhat, lahoras pren una agula en la qual haia fil e met aquela en le mieg de la figura, e entromet le autre fiel prop le lacrimal major, e·l fiel segon prop le lacrimal mendre, e ajusta entre les tieus ditz les fiels am equalitat, e aprop am aquels eleva la tua ma am elevacio engual, eleva tota la codena sobre la qual es senhat ayssi cum havem recomtat.	But if it is not possible to do so, having the threads, and this is not equivalent, then take a needle with thread and insert that in the middle of the figure, and then proceed with the other thread near the lacrimal major, and the second thread near the lacrimal minor, and adjust between the words of totality the threads with equality, and then lift your hand with equal lifting, lift the entire cord above which is marked as we have recounted.
E aprop ajusta las doas labias de la plagua am sutura, e cura aquel entro que sia sanat.	And then adjust the two lips of the wound with a suture, and cure that until it is healed.
Mays si accideys apostema deves la tua inscizio o la tua fissura, seda aquel apostema am cerot e a lu semblantz, e am enguentz.	But if there is an apostema caused by your incision or slit, settle that apostema with cerote and lukewarm water, and with ointments.
E alcunas veguadas endeve a la palpebra que·ls sieus pels sian convertitz, adonc cove que tu uses en aquela de aquo que havem dit de inscizio; mays sutura en quascus es mays artificial.	And some times it grows on the eyelid where their own hairs are converted, then it is good that you use in that of what we have said about incision; but suture in each case is more artificial.
Ataxinir am cannas es segon aquesta forma:	Taxinir by canals is according to this form:
e es que tu convertas la palpebra e scindas la figura qu’es dedintz segon que he recontat; e aprop per art fay doas cannas o doas astelas subtils de las quals longitut sia segon la longitut de la palpebra e la latitut de lor sia mendra de la latitut del spatum.	And it is that you convert the eyelid and cut the figure which is below according to what I have recounted; and then by art make two canals or two thin staves from which the length is according to the length of the eyelid and the width of their width is less than the width of the instrument.
E tu ja has inscidit en las extremitatz de quascunas partidas, la on tenes les fils.	And you have already incised at the extremities of each partition, where you have the threads.
Aprop agregua quascuna am subtilitat subre aquo que superflueys de la palpebra del huel, e constres las cannas de quascunas partidas am fort strictura, e layssa aquela per alcus jorns, quar la codena per la strictura morira e sira denegada e se poyrira entro que per si meteyssa cayra.	And then gather each one with subtlety over what superfluous of the eyelid of the eye, and tighten the canals of each partition with a strong constriction, and leave it for some days, because the cord will die and be rejected and will settle in until it falls into place.
Mays si es tardat, lahoras trenca la am las toroyras, e aprop cura la plagua entro que sia sanat.	But if it is delayed, then tear the cord apart with forceps, and then cure the wound until it is healed.
Donc cum es solidada, la palpebra es elevada e les pels no pungo.	Therefore when it is solidified, the eyelid is raised and the hairs do not sting.
E aquesta es la forma de doas cannas las quals faras segon aquesta forma:	And this is the form of two canals which you will make according to this form:
e haia la quantitat de la longitut e de la latitut ni mays ni mens.	and have the quantity of length and width neither more nor less.
Capitol .xii.	Chapter XII.
De elevacio de pels pungentz en le huel am agula quan le pel es dur.	On the Elevation of Stinging Hairs in the Eye with a Needle when the Hair is Hard.
Quan son pels no-naturals, durs e aspres e pungentz les huels, lahoras la operacio en lu es que tu prenguas agula subtil e pauses en aquela fiel de ceda subtil e leon, e aprop que tu ajustes las extremitatz de lu e nozes quascu en manieyra mot subtil.	When the hairs are unnatural, hard, and sharp, and sting the eyes, the operation in that is that you take a subtle needle and insert it into that thread of cedar and lion, and then adjust the extremities of it and note each one in a manner very subtle.
E sia la longitut dels fiels de quantitat de una palma.	And be the length of the threads of the quantity of one palm.
E aprop tu compon2 autre fiel subtil dejos lu en breu, e nuza las extremitatz de aquel si tu·t vols.	And then you compose another subtle thread below it in brief, and tie the extremities of that if you wish.
E aprop pause le malaute le sieu cap en le tieu se, e sia prop del solelh per que la tua obra sia declarada, quar es operacio subtil e menuda.	And then place the patient's head on the bed, and be near the sun so that your work may be declared, for it is a subtle and delicate operation.
E aprop intromet la agulha en la razit del pel ajustat la qual ha necessitat de engen, e fay aquela penetrar en la palpebra festinantment entro que extraguas aquela desus le pel natural.	And then insert the needle into the root of the hair adjusted to which it has been necessary to apply art, and make that penetrate into the eyelid quickly until you extract that above the natural hair.
E aprop tire le pel entro desus e intromet aquel en alixati, e sian les pels un o dos o tres e no mays.	And then pull out the hair above and insert it into its place, and be the hairs one, two, or three, but not more.
E aprop tira la tua ma am aquel entro que·l pel sia fora-gitat am alixolati en la palpebra am le pel natural.	And then pull out your hand with that until the hair is extricated and settled into its place in the eyelid with the natural hair.
Mays si es atirat alixalati e non es gitat le pel, atiraras alixati a las partidas dejos am le fiel le qual tu has compost am aquela, entro qu’en sia gitat alixalati del trau sobira.	But if it is attracted to the eyelid and not extracted the hair, you will attract the eyelid to the parts below with the thread which you have composed with that, until in it is extracted from the upper part of the brow.
E vegas aquela am la visio del huel, quar lahoras tu gitaras alixati e lo fiel, e grotan quascu e clautz le huel, e laysse le claus per dos dias o tres, entro que·l pel adheresca al sieu loc e nasque sobre aquel bona carn.	And behold that with the vision of the eye, for then you will extract the eyelid and the thread, and gently pluck out each and every one of them from the eye, and leave the closures for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place and grows over it good flesh.
E si es mays breu le pel, lahoras tu ajusta un pel lonc dels pels naturals, e es elevat am aquel, o que·l leysses entro que sia alonguat aprop alcu spazi, e lehoras tu eleva aquel.	And if the hair is shorter, then you will adjust one long hair from the natural hairs, and it is elevated with that, or so that it leaves space until it becomes long again, and then you will elevate that.
Capitol .xiii.	Chapter XIII.
De la cura de ehacratir la qual ve en la palpebra desus.	On the Cure for Cataract Which Appears in the Eyelid Above.
Quan ve en le huel ehacratir, e es contraccio de la palpebra quan es contrayta en sus, o a dextra o a sinistra partida, per mala consolidacio de plagua o de seccio o de cauteri, e es apelada leporina, e aquesta ahercrati o es natural o accidental, e es fayta per consolidacio de plagua o de seccios o de cauteri, o per semblantz a lor malcuratz.	When cataract appears in the eye, and it is contraction of the eyelid when it is constricted above or on one side or the other, due to bad consolidation of wound or section or cauterization, and it is called leporina, and this cataract either is natural or accidental, and it is caused by consolidation of wound or sections or cauterizations, or by likenesses to their maladies.
May la manieyra de la operacio en lu es que tu fendas aquela consolidacio e que separes las labias de lu, e pauses en lu en aquo que es entre aquelas una meca de drap de li, e ligues aquelas entro que sian sanadas.	The manner of the operation in that is that you will cut through that consolidation and separate the lips of it, and insert a piece of linen cloth between them, and tie those together until they are healed.
E no cove que tu uses de curacio de lu de las causas las quals exsiccan, constrenho; quar si tu fas aquo retorna alixacratir pus mal que nulh temps no foc habantz.	And it is not good that you use any cure of it from the causes which dry up and constrict; for if you do so, it will return to be worse than ever before, without any hope.
Usa en aquela de causas que mollifico ayssi cum es fenugrec, e embroca am la aygua en la qual son coytz altea e semensa de li, o enguent dyaquilon, le qual sia liquefayt am alcu dels olis, e submergeys en aquel la meca, e cura am aquel.	Use in that of causes which soften like fenugreek, and steep it in hot water where coriander is grown and sown with linseed, or a poultice of aquilon, which is liquefied with some oil, and submerge the cloth in that, and cure with that.
E lo tesaur de la tua curacio es que tu perforsses am tot engen que no sia consolidat segon la forma que foc al comensament.	And the treasure of your cure is that you perforate it with all art, and not be consolidated according to the form in which it began.
E aquesta operacio la qual havem dita, no es sino alcuna rectificacio de ehalixacrati que no retorna la forma del loc segon que foc denant.	And this operation which we have said, is nothing but some correction of cataract that does not return to its original form as it was before.
Capitol .xiiii.	Chapter XIV.
De la cura de ehacrati le qual es fayt en la palpebra dejos.	On the Cure for Cataract Which is Done in the Eyelid Below.
Aquesta alxacrati la qual es fayta en la palpebra dejos, la qual es nompnada vertadierament alxacrati; e es de lu alcuna natural, autra accidental.	This cataract which is made in the eyelid below, which is truly called vertadierament cataract; and it is of some natural origin, or other accidental.
Mays accidental es fayta per plagua o per scissura o per cauteri o per autres semblantz.	But accidental is made by wound or section or cauterization or by other likenesses.
E la via de la operacio de lu es que tu prenguas una agula en la qual haga fil doble, e fiques aquela en la carn, e que la fassas passar del lacrimal de senestre entro al lacrimal dextre, entro que·l fil pervengua en las doas extremitatz de la carn.	And the way of the operation for that is that you take a needle with double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left lacrimal to the right lacrimal, until the thread reaches the two extremities of the flesh.
E aprop exten la carn a las partidas desus am la agula e cus aquela am la agula, e inscideys am spatum ample.	And then stretch the flesh to the upper parts with the needle and cut it with the needle, and insert it into an instrument of broad width.
E donc si retorne la figura de la palpebre segon que cove, bo es; e sino, pren le ray e pausa aquel en la figura fenduda, e am aquel converteys la palpebra, e fen las doas fissuras en le latz de la palpebra dejos.	And therefore if the figure of the eyelid returns as it should, good is; and otherwise, take the thread and place that in the cleft figure, and with that convert the eyelid, and close the two slits on the side of the eyelid below.
E sian las extremitatz de las doas fissuras de dos angles de la inscizio, la qual has fayta entro que concurren, e sia de lor fayt angle entro que quan se congreguan sia fayta figura de lor.
